href="/wiki/Harness_racing" title="Harness racing">Harness racing</a> in <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a></figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_(2).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_%282%29.jpg/220px-Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_%282%29.jpg/330px-Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_%282%29.jpg/440px-Corsa_ippica_-_Palio_di_Legnano_2013_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a><figcaption>Wild Horse racing in <a href="/wiki/Palio_di_Legnano" title="Palio di Legnano">Palio di Legnano</a> 2013</figcaption></figure>\n<p><b>Horse racing</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> performance activity, typically involving two or more <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horses</a> ridden by <a href="/wiki/Jockey" title="Jockey">jockeys</a> (or sometimes driven without riders) over a set distance for competition. It is one of the most ancient of all sports, as its basic premise \xe2\x80\x93 to identify which of two or more horses is the fastest over a set course or distance \xe2\x80\x93 has been mostly unchanged since at least <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Horse races vary widely in format, and many countries have developed their own particular traditions around the sport. Variations include restricting races to particular <a href="/wiki/Breed" title="Breed">breeds</a>, running over obstacles, running over different distances, running on different <a href="/wiki/Track_surface" title="Track surface">track surfaces</a>, and running in different <a href="/wiki/Horse_gait" title="Horse gait">gaits</a>. In some races, horses are assigned different weights to carry to reflect differences in ability, a process known as handicapping.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>While horses are sometimes raced purely for sport, a major part of horse racing\'s interest and economic importance is in the <a href="/wiki/Betting_on_horse_racing" title="Betting on horse racing">gambling</a> associated with it,<sup id="cite_ref-GamblingImpactStudy_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GamblingImpactStudy-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> an activity that in 2019 generated a worldwide market worth around US$115&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="World_Championship">World Championship</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: World Championship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Horseracing_Authorities" class="mw-redirect" title="International Federation of Horseracing Authorities">International Federation of Horseracing Authorities</a> was founded in 1961 and 1983 but now (2024) have not an official World Horse Racing Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg/220px-Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg/330px-Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg/440px-Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault_-_Riderless_Racers_at_Rome_-_Walters_37189.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1333" /></a><figcaption><i>Riderless Racers at Rome</i> by <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9odore_G%C3%A9ricault" title="Th\xc3\xa9odore G\xc3\xa9ricault">Th\xc3\xa9odore G\xc3\xa9ricault</a>, 1817</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House,_London.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House%2C_London.png/220px-DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House%2C_London.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House%2C_London.png/330px-DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House%2C_London.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House%2C_London.png/440px-DV307_no.84_Horse_racing_near_Apsley_House%2C_London.png 2x" data-file-width="1391" data-file-height="867" /></a><figcaption>British nobility horse racing at <a href="/wiki/Apsley_House" title="Apsley House">Apsley House</a>, London c. 1850s</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Horse racing has a long and distinguished history and has been practiced in civilizations across the world since ancient times. Archaeological records indicate that horse racing occurred in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria_(region)" title="Syria (region)">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pre-Islamic_Arabia" title="Pre-Islamic Arabia">Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Egypt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LibraryIndex_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LibraryIndex-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also plays an important part of myth and legend, such as in the contest between the steeds of the god <a href="/wiki/Odin" title="Odin">Odin</a> and the giant <a href="/wiki/Hrungnir" title="Hrungnir">Hrungnir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">Norse mythology</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chariot_racing" title="Chariot racing">Chariot racing</a> was one of the most popular sports of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Rome</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. By 648 BCE, both chariot and mounted horse racing events were part of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Olympic_Games" title="Ancient Olympic Games">Greek Olympics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hellenism_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hellenism-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and were important in the other <a href="/wiki/Panhellenic_Games" title="Panhellenic Games">Panhellenic Games</a>. Chariot racing was dangerous to both driver and horse, often leading to serious injury and even death. In the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, chariot and mounted horse racing were major industries.<sup id="cite_ref-Rome_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rome-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From the mid-fifth century BCE, <a href="/wiki/Spring_carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Spring carnival">spring carnival</a> in Rome closed with a horse race. Fifteen to twenty riderless horses, originally imported from the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Coast" title="Barbary Coast">Barbary Coast</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, were set loose to run the length of the <a href="/wiki/Via_del_Corso" title="Via del Corso">Via del Corso</a>, a long, straight city street. The race lasted about two-and-a-half minutes.\n</p><p>In later times, <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a> racing became popular with British royalty and aristocrats, earning it the title of "Sport of Kings".<sup id="cite_ref-Specogna_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Specogna-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Historically, equestrians honed their skills through games and races. Equestrian sports provided entertainment for crowds and displayed the horsemanship required for battle. Horse racing evolved from impromptu competitions among riders and drivers. The various forms of competition, which required demanding and specialized skills from both horse and rider, resulted in the systematic development of specialized breeds and equipment. The popularity of equestrian sports throughout the centuries has resulted in the preservation of skills that would otherwise have vanished once horses were no longer used in combat.<sup id="cite_ref-Olsen_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olsen-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In Britain, horse racing became well-established in the 18th century, and continued to grow in popularity. <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II</a> (reigned 1649 to 1685) was an avid sportsman who gave <a href="/wiki/Newmarket_Racecourse" title="Newmarket Racecourse">Newmarket</a> its prominence. By 1750, the <a href="/wiki/Jockey_Club" title="Jockey Club">Jockey Club</a> was formed as a way to control the Newmarket races, set the rules of the game, prevent dishonesty, and create a level field.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Derby" title="Epsom Derby">Epsom Derby</a> began in 1780. <a href="/wiki/British_Classic_Races" title="British Classic Races">The first of the five classic races</a> began with the <a href="/wiki/St_Leger_Stakes" title="St Leger Stakes">St Leger Stakes</a> in 1776. In 1814, the system was complete with five annual races.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While Newmarket and the Jockey Club set the standards, most of the racing took place in landowners\' fields and in rising towns for small cash prizes and enormous local prestige. The system of wagering was essential to  funding and growing of the industry, and all classes, from paupers to royalty participated. Members of high society were in control, and they made a special effort to keep out the riff-raff and to keep the criminal element away from the wagering. With real money at stake, the system needed skilled jockeys, trainers, grooms, and experts at breeding, which opened up new careers for working-class rural men. Every young ambitious stable boy could dream of making it big.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to its rich history, horse racing is marked by noteworthy statistics. The Thoroughbred Secretariat still holds the fastest times in the 1973 Triple Crown races. Jockey Russell Baze demonstrated exceptional skill with an unmatched 12,842 victories. Economic significance is reflected in the career earnings of the American Pharoah, totaling over $8.6 million. These quantifiable achievements add another facet to the captivating history of horse racing."\n</p><p>Horse racing was one of the few sports that continued during the 2020 COVID-19 crisis,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with the Australian and Hong Kong racing jurisdictions carrying on, albeit with no crowds. The United States, the United Kingdom, and France were some of the more prominent racing bodies to either postpone or cancel all events.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Types_of_horse_racing">Types of horse racing</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Types of horse racing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are many types of horse racing, including:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Flat_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Flat racing">Flat racing</a></b>, where horses <a href="/wiki/Canter" class="mw-redirect" title="Canter">gallop</a> directly between two points around a straight or oval track.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Jump_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Jump racing">Jump racing</a></b>, or <b>Jumps racing</b>, also known as <b><a href="/wiki/Steeplechase_(horse_racing)" title="Steeplechase (horse racing)">Steeplechasing</a></b> or, in Great Britain and Ireland, <b><a href="/wiki/National_Hunt_racing" title="National Hunt racing">National Hunt racing</a></b>, where horses race over obstacles.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Harness_racing" title="Harness racing">Harness racing</a></b>, where horses <a href="/wiki/Horse_gait" title="Horse gait">trot or pace</a> while pulling a driver in a <a href="/wiki/Sulky" title="Sulky">sulky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdwards1994332\xe2\x80\x93337_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards1994332\xe2\x80\x93337-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Saddle Trotting, where horses must trot from a starting point to a finishing point under saddle</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Endurance_riding" title="Endurance riding">Endurance racing</a></b>, where horses travel across the country over extreme distances, generally ranging from 25 to 100 miles (40 to 161&#160;km). Anything less than 25 miles qualifies as a limited distance ride or LD.</li></ul>\n<p>Different <a href="/wiki/List_of_horse_breeds" title="List of horse breeds">breeds of horses</a> have been bred to excel in each of these disciplines. Breeds that are used for flat racing include the <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Quarter_Horse" title="American Quarter Horse">Quarter Horse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_horse" title="Arabian horse">Arabian</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Paint_Horse" title="American Paint Horse">Paint</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Appaloosa" title="Appaloosa">Appaloosa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USHorse_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USHorse-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jump racing breeds include the <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a> and <a href="/wiki/AQPS" title="AQPS">AQPS</a>. In harness racing, <a href="/wiki/Standardbred" title="Standardbred">Standardbreds</a> are used in Australia, New Zealand and North America. In Europe, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Trotter" title="Russian Trotter">Russian</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Trotter" title="French Trotter">French Trotters</a> are used with Standardbreds. Light cold blood horses, such as <a href="/wiki/Finnhorse" title="Finnhorse">Finnhorses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_coldblood_trotter" class="mw-redirect" title="Scandinavian coldblood trotter">Scandinavian Coldblood Trotters</a> are also used in harness racing within their respective geographical areas.\n</p><p>There are also races for ponies: both flat and jump<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and harness racing.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flat_racing">Flat racing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Flat racing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236091366">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Horse_racing" title="Special:EditPage/Horse racing">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2023</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Flat racing is the most common form of horse racing seen worldwide. Flat racing tracks are typically oval in shape and are generally level, although in Great Britain and Ireland there is much greater variation, including figure-of-eight tracks like <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Racecourse" title="Windsor Racecourse">Windsor</a> and tracks with often severe gradients and changes of camber, such as <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Racecourse" class="mw-redirect" title="Epsom Racecourse">Epsom Racecourse</a>. Track surfaces vary, with turf most common in Europe and dirt more common in North America and Asia. Newly designed synthetic surfaces, such as <a href="/wiki/Track_surface#Polytrack" title="Track surface">Polytrack</a> or <a href="/wiki/Track_surface#Tapeta" title="Track surface">Tapeta</a>, are seen at some tracks.\n</p><p>Individual flat races are run over distances ranging from 440 yards (400&#160;m) to more than four miles (6.4&#160;km), although races longer than two miles (3.2&#160;km) are quite rare, and distances between five and twelve furlongs (1.0 and 2.4&#160;km) are the most common. Short races are generally referred to as "sprints", while longer races are known as "routes" in the United States or "staying races" in Europe. Although fast acceleration ("a turn of foot") is usually required to win either type of race, in general sprints are seen as a test of speed, while long-distance races are seen as a test of stamina. The most prestigious flat races in the world, such as the <a href="/wiki/Prix_de_l%27Arc_de_Triomphe" title="Prix de l&#39;Arc de Triomphe">Prix de l\'Arc de Triomphe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cup" title="Melbourne Cup">Melbourne Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan_Cup" title="Japan Cup">Japan Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Derby" title="Epsom Derby">Epsom Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubai_World_Cup" title="Dubai World Cup">Dubai World Cup</a>, are run over distances in the middle of this range and are seen as tests of both speed and stamina to some extent.\n</p><p>In the most prestigious races, horses are generally allocated the same weight to carry for fairness, with allowances given to younger horses and female horses running against males. These races are called <a href="/wiki/Conditions_races" title="Conditions races">conditions races</a> and offer the biggest <a href="/wiki/Purse_(horseracing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Purse (horseracing)">purses</a>. There is another category of races called <a href="/wiki/Handicap_(horse_racing)" title="Handicap (horse racing)">handicap races</a> where each horse is assigned a different weight to carry based on its ability.<sup id="cite_ref-HRChannel_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRChannel-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Besides the weight they carry, horses\' performance can also be influenced by position relative to the inside barrier, sex, jockey, and training.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Jump_racing">Jump racing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jump racing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg/220px-Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg/330px-Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg/440px-Horses_jump_over_hurdle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="533" /></a><figcaption>Race horses hurdling at Bangor</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/National_Hunt_racing" title="National Hunt racing">National Hunt racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steeplechase_(horse_racing)" title="Steeplechase (horse racing)">Steeplechase (horse racing)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurdling_(horse_race)" title="Hurdling (horse race)">Hurdling (horse race)</a></div>\n<p>Jump (or jumps) racing in Great Britain and Ireland is known as <a href="/wiki/National_Hunt_racing" title="National Hunt racing">National Hunt racing</a> (although, confusingly, National Hunt racing also includes flat races taking place at jumps meetings; these are known as <a href="/wiki/National_Hunt_flat" class="mw-redirect" title="National Hunt flat">National Hunt flat</a> races). Jump racing can be subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Steeplechase_(horse_racing)" title="Steeplechase (horse racing)">steeplechasing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurdling_(horse_race)" title="Hurdling (horse race)">hurdling</a>, according to the type and size of obstacles being jumped. The word "steeplechasing" can also refer collectively to any type of jump race in certain racing jurisdictions, particularly in the United States.\n</p><p>Typically, horses progress to bigger obstacles and longer distances as they get older, so that a European jumps horse will tend to start in National Hunt flat races as a juvenile, move on to hurdling after a year or so, and then, if thought capable, move on to steeplechasing.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Harness_racing">Harness racing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Harness racing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harness_racing" title="Harness racing">Harness racing</a></div>\n<p>A type of racing where horses go around a track while pulling a sulky and a driver behind them. In this sport, Standardbreds are used. These horses are separated into two categories, trotters and pacers. Pacers move the legs on each side of their body in tandem, while trotters move their diagonal legs together. The latter are typically faster than the former due to the gaits used.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Occasionally a horse will break their gait into an actual canter or gallop. This could cause the loss of a race or even a disqualification.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Notable races include the Hambletonian and the Breeder\'s Crown series.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Saddle_trot_racing">Saddle trot racing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Saddle trot racing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ridden trot races are more common in places such as Europe and New Zealand. These horses are trotters who race on the flat under saddle with a jockey on their backs.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Endurance_racing">Endurance racing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Endurance racing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Endurance_riding" title="Endurance riding">Endurance riding</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG/220px-Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG/330px-Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG/440px-Suffolk_Downs_horse_racing.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3547" data-file-height="2365" /></a><figcaption>Suffolk Downs starting gate, East Boston, Massachusetts</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The length of an endurance race varies greatly. Some are very short, only ten miles, while other races can be up to one hundred miles. There are a few races that are even longer than one hundred miles and last multiple days.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These different lengths of races are divided into five categories: pleasure rides (10\xe2\x80\x9320 miles), non-competitive trail rides (21\xe2\x80\x9327 miles), competitive trail rides (20\xe2\x80\x9345 miles), progressive trail rides (25\xe2\x80\x9360 miles), and endurance rides (40\xe2\x80\x93100 miles in one day, up to 250 miles (400&#160;km) in multiple days).<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Because each race is very long, trails of natural terrain are generally used.\n</p><p>Contemporary organized <a href="/wiki/Endurance_riding" title="Endurance riding">endurance racing</a> began in California around 1955, and the first race marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Tevis_Cup" title="Tevis Cup">Tevis Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This race was a one-hundred-mile, one-day-long ride starting in <a href="/wiki/Squaw_Valley,_Placer_County,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Squaw Valley, Placer County, California">Squaw Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Placer_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Placer County">Placer County</a>, and ending in <a href="/wiki/Auburn,_California" title="Auburn, California">Auburn</a>. Founded in 1972, the American Endurance Ride Conference was the United States\' first national endurance riding association.<sup id="cite_ref-types_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-types-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The longest endurance race in the world is the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Derby" title="Mongol Derby">Mongol Derby</a>, which is 1,000&#160;km (620&#160;mi) long.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Breeds">Breeds</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Breeds"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Horse_breeding" title="Horse breeding">Horse breeding</a></div>\n<p>In most horse races, entry is restricted to certain breeds; that is, the horse must have a sire (father) and a dam (mother) who are studbook-approved individuals of whatever breed is racing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> For example, in a normal harness race, the horse\'s sire and dam must both be pure Standardbreds. The exception to this is in Quarter Horse racing, where an Appendix Quarter Horse may be considered eligible to race against (standard) Quarter Horses. The designation of "Appendix" refers to the addendum section, or Appendix, of the Official Quarter Horse registry. An Appendix Quarter Horse is a horse that has either one Quarter Horse parent and one parent of any other eligible breed (such as Thoroughbred, the most common Appendix cross), two parents that are registered Appendix Quarter Horses, or one parent that is a Quarter Horse and one parent that is an Appendix Quarter Horse. AQHA also issues a "Racing Register of Merit", which allows a horse to race on Quarter Horse tracks, but not be considered a Quarter Horse for breeding purposes (unless other requirements are met).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>A stallion who has won many races may be put up to <a href="/wiki/Stud_(animal)" title="Stud (animal)">stud</a> when he is retired. <a href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination" title="Artificial insemination">Artificial insemination</a> and <a href="/wiki/Embryo_transfer" title="Embryo transfer">embryo transfer</a> technology (allowed only in some breeds) have brought changes to the traditions and ease of breeding.\n</p><p>Pedigrees of stallions are recorded in various books and websites, such as <i>Weatherbys Stallion Book</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Australian_Stud_Book" title="Australian Stud Book">Australian Stud Book</a></i> and <i>Thoroughbred Heritage</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Thoroughbred"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a></div>\n<p>There are three founding sires that all Thoroughbreds can trace back to in the male line: the <a href="/wiki/Darley_Arabian" title="Darley Arabian">Darley Arabian</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Godolphin_Arabian" title="Godolphin Arabian">Godolphin Arabian</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Byerley_Turk" title="Byerley Turk">Byerley Turk</a>, named after their respective owners <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Darley" title="Thomas Darley">Thomas Darley</a>, Lord Godolphin, and Captain Robert Byerly. They were taken to England, where they were bred with mares from English and imported bloodlines.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The resultant foals were the first generation of thoroughbreds, and all modern thoroughbreds are their descents. Thoroughbreds range in height, which is measured in <a href="/wiki/Hand_(unit)" title="Hand (unit)">hands</a> (a hand being four inches). Some are as small as 15 hands while others are over 17. Thoroughbreds can travel medium distances at fast paces, requiring a balance between speed and endurance. Thoroughbreds may be <a href="/wiki/Bay_(horse)" title="Bay (horse)">bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_(horse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black (horse)">black</a>, dark bay/brown, <a href="/wiki/Chestnut_(coat)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chestnut (coat)">chestnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gray_(horse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gray (horse)">gray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roan_(horse)" title="Roan (horse)">roan</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_(horse)" class="mw-redirect" title="White (horse)">white</a> or <a href="/wiki/Palomino" title="Palomino">palomino</a>. Artificial insemination, cloning and embryo transfer are not allowed in the Thoroughbred breed.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Harness_Racers_(21766576679).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Harness_Racers_%2821766576679%29.jpg/220px-Harness_Racers_%2821766576679%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Harness_Racers_%2821766576679%29.jpg/330px-Harness_Racers_%2821766576679%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Harness_Racers_%2821766576679%29.jpg/440px-Harness_Racers_%2821766576679%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1000" /></a><figcaption>Standardbred horses harness racing</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Standardbred">Standardbred</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Standardbred"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Standardbred" title="Standardbred">Standardbred</a></div>\n<p>The standardbred is a breed of horse used for a variety of purposes, but they are largely bred for harness racing. They are descended from thoroughbreds, morgans, and extinct breeds. Standardbreds are typically docile and easy to handle. They do not spook easily and are quite versatile in what they can do. They can be jumpers, dressage, and pleasure riding horses.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Arabian_horse">Arabian horse</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Arabian horse"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Arabian_horse" title="Arabian horse">Arabian horse</a></div>\n<p>The Arabian horse was developed by the <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> people of the West Asia specifically for stamina over long distances, so they could outrun their enemies. It was not until 1725 that the first Arabians was brought to North America,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and not until about the time of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> that they were bred as purebreds. Until the formation of the Arabian Horse Registry of America in 1908, Arabians were recorded with the <a href="/wiki/Jockey_Club" title="Jockey Club">Jockey Club</a> in a separate subsection from Thoroughbreds.\n</p><p>Arabians must be able to withstand traveling long distances at a moderate pace. They have an abundance of type I <a href="/wiki/Myocyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Myocyte">muscle fibers</a>, enabling their muscles to work for extended periods of time. Also, the muscles of the Arabian are not nearly as massive as those of the Quarter Horse, which allow it to travel longer distances at quicker speeds. The Arabian is primarily used today in <a href="/wiki/Endurance_riding" title="Endurance riding">endurance racing</a> but is also raced over traditional race tracks in many countries.\n</p><p>Arabian Horse Racing is governed by the International Federation of Arabian Horse Racing.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Quarter_Horse">Quarter Horse</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Quarter Horse"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Quarter_Horse" title="American Quarter Horse">American Quarter Horse</a></div>\n<p>The ancestors of the Quarter Horse were prevalent in America in the early 17th century. These horses were a blend of <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Spanish_horse" title="Colonial Spanish horse">Colonial Spanish horses</a> crossed with English horses that were brought over in the 1700s. The native horse and the English horse were bred together, resulting in a compact, muscular horse. At this time, they were mainly used for chores such as plowing and cattle work. The American Quarter Horse was not recognized as an official breed until the formation of the <a href="/wiki/American_Quarter_Horse_Association" title="American Quarter Horse Association">American Quarter Horse Association</a> in 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In order to be successful in racing, Quarter Horses need to be able to propel themselves forward at extremely fast sprinter speed. The Quarter Horse has much larger hind limb muscles than the Arabian, which make it less suitable for endurance racing.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also has more type II-b muscle fibers, which allow the Quarter Horse to accelerate rapidly.\n</p><p>When Quarter Horse racing began, it was very expensive to lay a full mile of track so it was agreed that a straight track of four hundred meters, or one-quarter of a mile, would be laid instead.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It became the standard racing distance for Quarter Horses and inspired their name. With the exception of the longer, 870-yard (800&#160;m) distance contests, Quarter Horse races are run flat out, with the horses running at top speed for the duration. There is less jockeying for position, as turns are rare, and many races end with several contestants grouped together at the wire. The track surface is similar to that of Thoroughbred racing and usually consists of dirt.\n</p><p>In addition to the three main racing breeds above and their crosses, horse racing may be conducted using various other breeds: Appaloosa, American Paint Horse, <a href="/wiki/Selle_Fran%C3%A7ais" title="Selle Fran\xc3\xa7ais">Selle Fran\xc3\xa7ais</a>, AQPS<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Korean <a href="/wiki/Jeju_horse" title="Jeju horse">Jeju</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Horse_breeds_and_muscle_structure">Horse breeds and muscle structure</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Horse breeds and muscle structure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Muscles are bundles of contractile fibers that are attached to bones by tendons. These bundles have different types of fibers within them, and horses have adapted over the years to produce different amounts of these fibers.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Type_1">Type 1</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Type 1"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Type I muscle fibers are adapted for <a href="/wiki/Cellular_respiration#Aerobic_respiration" title="Cellular respiration">aerobic</a> exercise and rely on the presence of oxygen. They are slow-twitch fibers. They allow muscles to work for longer periods of time resulting in greater endurance.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Type_2">Type 2</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Type 2"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Type II muscles are adapted for <a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_exercise" title="Anaerobic exercise">anaerobic exercise</a> because they can function in the absence of oxygen.\n</p><p>Type II-a fibers are intermediate, representing a balance between the fast-twitch fibers and the slow-twitch fibers. They allow the muscles to generate both speed and endurance. Thoroughbreds possess more Type II-a muscle fibers than Quarter Horses or Arabians. This type of fiber allows them to propel themselves forward at great speeds and maintain it for an extended distance.\n</p><p>Type II-b fibers are fast-twitch fibers. These fibers allow muscles to contract quickly, resulting in a great deal of power and speed.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Training">Training</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Training"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-James_Pollard_-_The_Derby_Pets-_The_Winner_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5105" data-file-height="3641" /></a><figcaption><i>The <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Derby" title="Epsom Derby">Derby</a> Pets - The Winner</i>; painting by <a href="/wiki/James_Pollard" title="James Pollard">James Pollard</a>, c. 1840</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The conditioning program for the horses varies depending on the race length. Genetics, training, age, and skeletal soundness are all factors that contribute to a horse\'s performance.<sup id="cite_ref-training_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-training-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The muscle structure and fiber type of horses depends on the breed; therefore, genetics must be considered when constructing a conditioning plan. A horse\'s fitness plan must be coordinated properly in order to prevent injury or lameness. If these are to occur, they may negatively affect a horse\'s willingness to learn.<sup id="cite_ref-training_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-training-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Sprinting exercises are appropriate for training two-year-old racehorses, but the number is limited by psychological factors as well as physical.<sup id="cite_ref-training_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-training-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A horse\'s skeletal system adapts to the exercise it receives. Because the skeletal system does not reach full maturity until the horse is at least six years of age, young racehorses often suffer injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-training_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-training-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Horse_racing_by_continent">Horse racing by continent</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Horse racing by continent"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="North_America">North America</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: North America"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="United_States">United States</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: United States"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing_in_the_United_States" title="Horse racing in the United States">Horse racing in the United States</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Race_Meeting_at_Jacksonville,_Alabama_by_W.S._Hedges_-_BMA.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/A_Race_Meeting_at_Jacksonville%2C_Alabama_by_W.S._Hedges_-_BMA.jpg/220px-A_Race_Meeting_at_Jacksonville%2C_Alabama_by_W.S._Hedges_-_BMA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="mw-file-element" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/A_Race_Meeting_at_Jacksonville%2C_Alabama_by_W.S._Hedges_-_BMA.jpg/440px-A_Race_Meeting_at_Jacksonville%2C_Alabama_by_W.S._Hedges_-_BMA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="681" /></a><figcaption>Horse racing at Jacksonville, Alabama, 1841</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_track_at_fairgrounds,_Toledo,_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_(page_1).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Race_track_at_fairgrounds%2C_Toledo%2C_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_%28page_1%29.jpg/220px-Race_track_at_fairgrounds%2C_Toledo%2C_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_%28page_1%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Race_track_at_fairgrounds%2C_Toledo%2C_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_%28page_1%29.jpg/330px-Race_track_at_fairgrounds%2C_Toledo%2C_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_%28page_1%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Race_track_at_fairgrounds%2C_Toledo%2C_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_%28page_1%29.jpg/440px-Race_track_at_fairgrounds%2C_Toledo%2C_O._-_DPLA_-_c70272485bd187fb7697c77c138906b8_%28page_1%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4102" data-file-height="2533" /></a><figcaption>Horse racing at Toledo, Ohio, 1910</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:DEGAN_Gabin_(_gani%27s_party_).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/DEGAN_Gabin_%28_gani%27s_party_%29.jpg/220px-DEGAN_Gabin_%28_gani%27s_party_%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/DEGAN_Gabin_%28_gani%27s_party_%29.jpg/330px-DEGAN_Gabin_%28_gani%27s_party_%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/DEGAN_Gabin_%28_gani%27s_party_%29.jpg/440px-DEGAN_Gabin_%28_gani%27s_party_%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8000" data-file-height="6037" /></a><figcaption>Horse race in Benin, Africa)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the United States, Thoroughbred flat races are run on surfaces of either dirt, synthetic or turf. Other tracks offer <a href="/wiki/American_Quarter_Horse" title="American Quarter Horse">Quarter Horse</a> racing and <a href="/wiki/Standardbred_horse" class="mw-redirect" title="Standardbred horse">Standardbred</a> racing, on combinations of these three types of racing surfaces. Racing of other breeds, such as Arabian horse racing, is found on a limited basis. American Thoroughbred races are run at a wide variety of distances, most commonly from 5 to 12 furlongs (0.63 to 1.50&#160;mi; 1.0 to 2.4&#160;km); with this in mind, breeders of Thoroughbred race horses attempt to breed horses that excel at a particular distance (see <a href="/wiki/Dosage_Index" title="Dosage Index">dosage index</a>).\n</p><p>Horse racing in the United States and on the North American continent dates back to 1665, which saw the establishment of the Newmarket course in Salisbury, New York, a section of what is now known as the Hempstead Plains of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This first racing meet in North America was supervised by New York\'s colonial governor, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nicolls" title="Richard Nicolls">Richard Nicolls</a>. The area is now occupied by the present <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_New_York" title="Nassau County, New York">Nassau County, New York</a>, a region of Greater <a href="/wiki/Westbury,_New_York" title="Westbury, New York">Westbury</a> and East Garden City. The South Westbury section is still known as Salisbury.\n</p><p>The first record of quarter-mile length races dated back to 1674 in <a href="/wiki/Henrico_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Henrico County">Henrico County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>. Each race consisted of only two horses, and they raced down the village streets and lanes. The Quarter Horse received its name from the length of the race.\n</p><p>Tracing back the history of horse racing in the United States to its earliest inception in 1665, this sport has become an industry contributing approximately $15 billion to the U.S. economy today.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Horse racing has become the second most popular <a href="/wiki/Spectator_sport" title="Spectator sport">spectator sport</a> in the United States with the establishment of historic tracks like Belmont Park, major events like the Kentucky Derby, and significant institutions such as the American Stud Book.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Stud_Book" title="American Stud Book">American Stud Book</a> was started in 1868, prompting the beginning of organized horse racing in the United States. There were 314 tracks operating in the United States by 1890; and in 1894, the American Jockey Club was formed.<sup id="cite_ref-history_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pleasanton_Fairgrounds_Racetrack" title="Pleasanton Fairgrounds Racetrack">Pleasanton Fairgrounds Racetrack</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Alameda_County_Fairgrounds" title="Alameda County Fairgrounds">Alameda County Fairgrounds</a> is the oldest remaining horse racing track in America,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> dating from 1858, when it was founded by the sons of the Spaniard Don Agust\xc3\xadn Bernal.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Belmont_Park" title="Belmont Park">Belmont Park</a> is located at the western edge of the Hempstead Plains. Its mile-and-a-half main track is the largest dirt Thoroughbred racecourse in the world, and it has the sport\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Grandstand" title="Grandstand">grandstand</a>.\n</p><p>One of the latest major horse tracks opened in the United States was the <a href="/wiki/Meadowlands_Racetrack" title="Meadowlands Racetrack">Meadowlands Racetrack</a>, opened in 1977 for Thoroughbred and Harness racing. It is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Meadowlands_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Meadowlands Cup">Meadowlands Cup</a>. Other more recently opened tracks include <a href="/wiki/Remington_Park" title="Remington Park">Remington Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a>, opened in 1988, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houston_Race_Park" title="Sam Houston Race Park">Sam Houston Race Park</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> metro area, opened in 1994, and <a href="/wiki/Lone_Star_Park" title="Lone Star Park">Lone Star Park</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas\xe2\x80\x93Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas\xe2\x80\x93Fort Worth Metroplex</a>, opened in 1997; the latter track hosted the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Breeders%27_Cup" title="Breeders&#39; Cup">Breeders\' Cup</a> series of races in 2004.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_horse_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Thoroughbred horse racing">Thoroughbred horse racing</a> in the United States has its own <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Racing_and_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Museum of Racing and Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_Springs,_New_York" title="Saratoga Springs, New York">Saratoga Springs, New York</a>. The Hall of Fame honors remarkable horses, jockeys, owners, and trainers.\n</p><p>The traditional high point of US horse racing is the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a>, held on the first Saturday of May at <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Downs" title="Churchill Downs">Churchill Downs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville, Kentucky</a>. Together, the Derby; the <a href="/wiki/Preakness_Stakes" title="Preakness Stakes">Preakness Stakes</a>, held two weeks later at <a href="/wiki/Pimlico_Race_Course" title="Pimlico Race Course">Pimlico Race Course</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, Maryland; and the <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Stakes" title="Belmont Stakes">Belmont Stakes</a>, held three weeks after the Preakness at <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Park" title="Belmont Park">Belmont Park</a> on Long Island, form the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Triple_Crown_of_Thoroughbred_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing">Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing</a> for three-year-olds. They are all held early in the year, throughout May and the beginning of June. In recent years the <a href="/wiki/Breeders%27_Cup" title="Breeders&#39; Cup">Breeders\' Cup</a> races, run at the end of the year, have challenged the Triple Crown events as determiners of the three-year-old champion. The Breeders\' Cup is normally held at a different track every year; however, the 2010 and 2011 editions were both held at Churchill Downs, and 2012, 2013 and 2014 races were held at <a href="/wiki/Santa_Anita_Park" title="Santa Anita Park">Santa Anita Park</a>. <a href="/wiki/Keeneland" title="Keeneland">Keeneland</a>, in Lexington, Kentucky, hosted the 2015 Breeders\' Cup.\n</p><p>The corresponding Standardbred event is the <a href="/wiki/Breeders_Crown" title="Breeders Crown">Breeders Crown</a>. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Harness_Racing_for_Pacers" class="mw-redirect" title="Triple Crown of Harness Racing for Pacers">Triple Crown of Harness Racing for Pacers</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Harness_Racing_for_Trotters" class="mw-redirect" title="Triple Crown of Harness Racing for Trotters">Triple Crown of Harness Racing for Trotters</a>.\n</p><p>American betting on horse racing is sanctioned and regulated by the state where the race is located.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Simulcast betting exists across state lines with minimal oversight except the companies involved through legalized <a href="/wiki/Parimutuel_gambling" class="mw-redirect" title="Parimutuel gambling">parimutuel gambling</a>. A takeout, or "take", is removed from each <a href="/wiki/Betting_pool" title="Betting pool">betting pool</a> and distributed according to state law, among the state, race track and horsemen. A variety of factors affect takeout, namely location and the type of wager that is placed.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One form of parimutuel gaming is <a href="/wiki/Instant_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Instant Racing">Instant Racing</a>, in which players bet on video replays of races.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Advanced_Deposit_Wagering" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Deposit Wagering">Advanced Deposit Wagering</a> is a form of gambling on the outcome of horse races in which the bettor must fund his or her account before being allowed to place bets. ADW is often conducted online or by phone. In contrast to ADW, credit shops allow wagers without advance funding; accounts are settled at month-end. Racetrack owners, horse trainers and state governments sometimes receive a cut of ADW revenues.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Canada">Canada</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Horse_racing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Canada"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The most famous horse from Canada is generally considered to be <a href="/wiki/Northern_Dancer" title="Northern Dancer">Northern Dancer</a>, who after winning the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a>, Preakness and Queen\'s Plate in 1964 went on to become the most successful Thoroughbred sire of the twentieth century; his two-minute-flat Derby was the fastest on record until <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_(horse)" title="Secretariat (horse)">Secretariat</a> in 1973. The only challenger to his title of greatest Canadian horse would be his son <a href="/wiki/Nijinsky_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Nijinsky II">Nijinsky II</a>, who is the last horse to win the English <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Thoroughbred_Racing" title="Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing">Triple Crown</a>. <a href="/wiki/Woodbine_Racetrack" title="Woodbine Racetrack">Woodbine Racetrack</a> (1956) in Toronto is home of the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Plate">Queen\'s Plate</a> (1860), Canada\'s premier Thoroughbred stakes race, and the <a href="/wiki/North_America_Cup" title="North America Cup">North America Cup</a> (1984), Canada\'s premier Standardbred stakes race. It is the only race track in North America which stages Thoroughbred and Standardbred (harness) meetings on the same day. The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_International_Stakes" title="Canadian International Stakes">Canadian International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodbine_Mile" title="Woodbine Mile">Woodbine Mile</a> (1981) are Canada\'s most important Grade I races worth <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">Can$</a>1,000,000 each, and have been won by many renowned horses such as <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_(horse)" title="Secretariat (horse)">Secretariat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wise_Dan" title="Wise Dan">Wise Dan</a> respectively. Other key races include <a href="/wiki/Woodbine_Oaks" title="Woodbine Oaks">Woodbine Oaks</a> (1956), <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Stakes" title="Prince of Wales Stakes">Prince of Wales Stakes</a> (1929), <a href="/wiki/Breeders%27_Stakes" title="Breeders&#39; Stakes">Breeders\' Stakes</a> (1889) and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Derby" title="Canadian Derby">Canadian Derby</a> (1930).\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pierwsze_wy%C5%9Bcigi_w_Warszawie_(59465).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img
